  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_4343703d-1bf7-4ef3-80a8-ec568fef94d8'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1648664090" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6141085122740902893">Think this is one of the most powerful books I have ever read! I love all of Lesley's books, they are emotional, intriguing, passionate and full of suspense. This one in particular brought tears to my eyes and I could not put it down at all, it has stayed with me for years and I plan to read it again, something I never do. I passed it on to friend who also thought it was beyond excellent! I can't recommend this book if you are into powerful suspenseful family sagas! </span>

          </span>

<div id="review_174864348" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/174864348" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/174864348?book_show_action=true">Jun 08, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anna" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anna" href="/user/show/5594112-anna">Anna</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer174864348" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9647213765411345429">I read this book a couple of months ago. Now, I have a dreadful memory and normally forget about a book as soon as I've finished the next one, but this one has stuck in my mind as one to recommend to all. It is based on the true story of a woman convict called Mary, who is put on one of the first fleets to Australia. She has to go through so much to survive and even now I still feel moved by her plight. It puts my everyday problems into perspective that's for sure. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1502863207" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1502863207" />
    <a title="Nadira" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/51241595-nadira"><img alt="Nadira" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1452254734p2/51241595.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1502863207?book_show_action=true">Jan 09, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nadira" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nadira" href="/user/show/51241595-nadira">Nadira</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/51241595-nadira?shelf=owned-books">owned-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1502863207" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12539692664650916864">#toptenfavoritebooks: Remember Me by Leslie Pearse.<br/>.<br/>#NadirasPointOfReview: If you love #HistoricalFiction, pick this one up. If you love #TrueStories & #Memoirs, pick this up! If you love books that will pull at ur heart strings, pick it up NOW! There really are not enough words to describe how much I love this book. It has a GR rating of 4.29. I've recommended/gifted it to so many people who have also enjoyed it. I got myself a copy recently & I cant wait to re-read it again sometime.<br/>. <br/>This is </span>
  <span id="freeText12539692664650916864" style="display:none">#toptenfavoritebooks: Remember Me by Leslie Pearse.<br />.<br />#NadirasPointOfReview: If you love #HistoricalFiction, pick this one up. If you love #TrueStories &amp; #Memoirs, pick this up! If you love books that will pull at ur heart strings, pick it up NOW! There really are not enough words to describe how much I love this book. It has a GR rating of 4.29. I've recommended/gifted it to so many people who have also enjoyed it. I got myself a copy recently &amp; I cant wait to re-read it again sometime.<br />. <br />This is a remarkable true story of a young girl from Cornwall in England named Mary Broad who is convicted &amp; sentenced to death for a petty theft. But instead she is transported to Australia as a prisoner. The story is enjoyable &amp; captivating; historically enlightening. It takes you on a gripping sea voyage with the first fleet of convicts to Australia. The journey delves deep into the early days of these convicts...the first settlement in the country...How they had to struggle against appalling conditions to make the land viable for survival &amp; living...and the hardships they endured.<br />.<br />Although it is a long story, it is unputdownable - you will simply wish it to never end. This emotionally-draining book is an adventurous read. I loved the story, the characters, the excitement of the journey. It had its heart-breaking moments that made me cry RIVERS literally. You cannot fail to be affected by the story of Mary Broad and you mourn and rejoice with her. You laugh and you cry with her. Definitely one of my top favorite books and I highly recommend it. Honestly the best book I've ever read. 5</span>
  <a data-text-id="12539692664650916864" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText7523405421913772401" style="display:none">I loved this book! I have now read three books by Lesley Pearse and I am amazed at how very different they are. Remember me is a novel based on a true story and so I found myself not only enjoying the story but also learning such a lot. Although I knew that Australia was once a destination for convicts I had no idea of the conditions on the voyage or the hardships that those on the first fleet endured. You cannot fail to be affected by the story of Mary Broad and you mourn and rejoice with her along her journey.I would recommend this book to everyone, especially if you have a love of history and like me can't resist an incredible story.</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1824766142" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1824766142" />
    <a title="Mad" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30312601-mad"><img alt="Mad" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1518179416p2/30312601.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1824766142?book_show_action=true">Nov 29, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mad" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mad" href="/user/show/30312601-mad">Mad</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9789892303178" href="/book/show/6298008-nunca-me-esque-as">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1824766142" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6414298886586421792">4/5* <br/><br/>Full review (PT & ENG): <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://presa-nas-palavras.blogspot.pt/2017/11/nunca-me-esquecasremember-me-opiniao.html'>http://presa-nas-palavras.blogspot.pt...</a><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1512748650i/24630027.png' width='250' height='320' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>ENG: I decided to read a Lesley Pearse book hoping it would be one of those cute romances everybody talks about. However, and without me knowing, I chose one of her books that do not fit it that category. In fact, I had never read such a violent book in my life.<br/>Remember Me is the title of the true story of Mary Broad, a woman sentenced of deportation by theft to Australia, in a reintegration project founded by England to popula</span>
  <span id="freeText6414298886586421792" style="display:none">4/5* <br><br>Full review (PT &amp; ENG): <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://presa-nas-palavras.blogspot.pt/2017/11/nunca-me-esquecasremember-me-opiniao.html">http://presa-nas-palavras.blogspot.pt...</a><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1512748650i/24630027.png" width="250" height="320" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>ENG: I decided to read a Lesley Pearse book hoping it would be one of those cute romances everybody talks about. However, and without me knowing, I chose one of her books that do not fit it that category. In fact, I had never read such a violent book in my life.<br>Remember Me is the title of the true story of Mary Broad, a woman sentenced of deportation by theft to Australia, in a reintegration project founded by England to populate this area. Mary was known as the first person to organise and participate in a well-succeeded escape from the penal colony. In that escape there were her husband, seven men and her two small children besides her. They were able to travel through around 5 000kms on a sailing boat in open sea. The book follows the protagonist since she leaves her parents’ house until the moment of the theft, including the violent boat trip, the horror in Australia, the intricate escape, the death of the children, her husband and people she considered family among other problems.<br>What I feel is that this book and this story don’t have the protagonism that it should, since it tells something so exceptional. I had never heard of this, not even on History classes.<br>In the beginning, is was really hard for me to get into the story. I didn’t understand some action, it wasn’t what I had expected and so I wasn’t that engaged. Nonetheless, as I kept reading, I got involved in this story in such a way that I finished the book with an urge to cry. The author’s work was really good, her descriptions and the way she wrote it can touch even the coldest of people. It is a good book, yes. But it’s a book that I don’t ever want to read again in this lifetime. The violence of the book and knowing that the plot’s events are real create a pain in the heart in such a way that it stays with you until you read the author’s final notes.<br>(CAREFUL: This part might be considered spoilers, even though it’s just historical events) The end of the book did not help my pain. The story ends in an open way, since there are no more records of what actually happened to Mary Broad up to a certain point of her life. Just like the author says in her final notes, it is possible that she didn’t resign to a quiet, placid life and made great thing out of her life. But we don’t know, and that’s the worst part. Through the span of over 400 pages, I connected to a real woman, I suffered with her and supported her, but now I don’t even know when she died or in what country. And that uncertainty is the problem of real stories: we don’t have a happy ending or a closed one. We have the doubt that will always be with you. I just hope that everything went well and that finally God, or whatever entity governs us, had opened their eyes to this incredible woman and mother whose story should never be forgotten.<br>The title of this book is Remember Me and it is, without a doubt, an unforgettable story.<br>With this said, I think it’s obvious that I recommend this book.<br><br>---<br><br>PT: Decidi ler um livro da Lesley Pearse na esperança de que fosse mais um daqueles romances fofos e seguros de que toda a gente fala. No entanto, e sem eu saber, escolhi exatamente um dos poucos livros dela que não o é. Pelo contrário, é uma das histórias mais violentas com que já me deparei.<br>Nunca Me Esqueças é o título da história verídica de Mary Broad, uma mulher condenada por roubo à deportação para a Austrália naquele que era um projeto de reintegração criado pela Inglaterra para povoar esta zona. Mary ficou conhecida por ter sido a primeira mulher a organizar e participar numa fuga bem sucedida da colónia penal em que se encontrava, fuga essa composta por ela, os seus dois filhos pequenos, o marido e mais sete homens, sendo que eles conseguiram viajar por cerca de 5000 km num barco à vela em mar aberto. Este livro acompanha a protagonista desde que sai de casa dos pais, até ao momento do roubo, a viagem violenta no barco, o terror na Austrália e a fuga complicada, entre muitos outros problemas que surgiram pelo caminho.<br>Depois de ler esta história, fiquei automaticamente com vontade de saber até que ponto era verdadeira, uma vez que nunca tinha ouvido nada sobre a mesma, e fiquei surpreendida ao perceber que é, de facto, na sua maioria, verídica, o que me deixou a sentir que este livro e a história dela não têm o protagonismo que deviam tendo em conta que foi algo tão excecional e da qual ninguém ouve falar. <br>O título original deste livro é Remember Me, que eu achei que podia ser traduzido de uma forma melhor, mais não seja para não dar a esta história um ar tão de romance.<br>A princípio eu custei realmente a entrar na história, não percebia certas ações, não era o que eu esperava e não tinha grande interesse. No entanto, com o passar das páginas, eu realmente envolvi-me nesta história e sofria com as personagens. Terminei o livro com vontade de chorar, o trabalho que a autora fez foi muito bom, as suas descrições e a forma como escreveu conseguem tocar até a mais fria das pessoas. É um livro bom sim, mas também é um livro que nunca mais quero ler na minha vida: a violência do livro e, pior, saber que os acontecimentos na base da ação são verdade, criam uma dor no coração de tal forma que nos acompanha ainda enquanto lemos as notas finais da autora.<br>(Atenção que isto pode ser considerado spoilers, apesar de o que vou referir ser histórico) O final do livro só ajudou na minha dor. A história termina de forma aberta, já que a partir daí não há mais registos sobre o que aconteceu com a Mary Broad. Como a própria autora diz nas suas notas finais, é possível que ela não se tenha resignado a uma vida pacata e tenha feito ainda grandes coisas na vida, mas nós não sabemos, e isso ainda é o pior, passei mais de 400 páginas a ligar-me a uma personagem, a sofrer com ela e a torcer por ela. E terminei assim, não se sabe o ano em que morreu ou sequer o país, e é essa incerteza, por uma pessoa/personagem a quem me afeiçoei, que aperta ainda mais o coração. Concluo a dizer que este é o problema de histórias verídicas: não temos o final feliz ou o final em fechado, temos a incerteza que provavelmente me vai acompanhar para sempre, só espero que tudo lhe tenha corrido bem e que, finalmente, Deus, ou quem quer que nos governe, tenha aberto os olhos para esta fantástica mulher e mãe de quem a história nunca se devia de esquecer.<br>Acho que nem preciso de dizer que recomendo. Boas leituras.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6414298886586421792" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1520658197" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9318178076413206052">Time taken to read - 2 days<br/><br/>Pages - 543<br/><br/>Publisher - Penguin<br/><br/>Blurb from Goodreads<br/><br/>She made a mistake and now she'll never see home again....<br/><br/>Mary, a Cornish mariner's daughter made the biggest mistake of her short life when she steals a silk hat. Convicted and sentenced to be transported to Australia, she endures horific conditions aboard the ship before landing in a brutal and barbaric country<br/><br/>It will take all her courage just to survive.<br/><br/>But Mary is also determined to make something of herself in this</span>
  <span id="freeText9318178076413206052" style="display:none">Time taken to read - 2 days<br /><br />Pages - 543<br /><br />Publisher - Penguin<br /><br />Blurb from Goodreads<br /><br />She made a mistake and now she'll never see home again....<br /><br />Mary, a Cornish mariner's daughter made the biggest mistake of her short life when she steals a silk hat. Convicted and sentenced to be transported to Australia, she endures horific conditions aboard the ship before landing in a brutal and barbaric country<br /><br />It will take all her courage just to survive.<br /><br />But Mary is also determined to make something of herself in this rugged man's world. And she dreams that one day she will find a way of crossing the cruel sea that lie between her and home....<br /><br />Based on a true story, Remember Me brings Mary Broad vividly to life in this moving story of a women triumphing against overwhelming odds.<br /><br /><br /><br />My Review<br /><br />Based on a true story, Mary Broad brings to life the horrors that a somewhat trivial crime could bring about in that period of time. 1786, shy of her twentieth birthday, Mary is sentenced to death by hanging, for the crime of stealing a silk hat. Spared her death sentence, she is sentenced to be shipped to Australia to live out her sentence and be put to work. From sentencing, the journey across the sea and eventually landing on the shore and the colony to work and fight for survival. <br /><br />I am not a huge fan of historical fiction however Pearse has a way with words and draws the reader in quickly, vested in the character you need to keep reading to see how she fares. The conditions Mary faces is horrendous, mixed with other criminals rape and violence are rife. Struggling to survive, get her share of rations, keep away from the body fluids building up in an enclosed filthy environment, Mary uses her wits and all available resources.<br /><br />It is hard hitting at times, some of the things Mary either sees or endures makes for uncomfortable reading. We experience relationships, betrayal, love, loss, adult and children dying as well as the casual attitude to death as such a common occurrence. This book packs a punch and will take you on an emotional roller coaster. I have read this author before and I will read her again, 4/5 for me this time.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9318178076413206052" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Dark-Draco" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18484922-dark-draco"><img alt="Dark-Draco" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1363942329p2/18484922.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3255761267?book_show_action=true">Apr 02, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dark-Draco" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dark-Draco" href="/user/show/18484922-dark-draco">Dark-Draco</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780141046082" href="/book/show/7934411-remember-me">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18484922-dark-draco?shelf=historic-fiction">historic-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3255761267" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2770791511075059733">So, this is the first book I have read by this author ... and I will definitely be returning to read more. This isn't usually my sort of genre, but I was instantly drawn to Mary and her fall from grace. It's a harrowing, heart-breaking story - I defy you not to cry as she loses those closest to her - and there's no final apology from the author. This is what happened back then, this is how criminals were treated, and she isn't going to sugar-coat it for modern readers. There's a happy ending of </span>
  <span id="freeText2770791511075059733" style="display:none">So, this is the first book I have read by this author ... and I will definitely be returning to read more. This isn't usually my sort of genre, but I was instantly drawn to Mary and her fall from grace. It's a harrowing, heart-breaking story - I defy you not to cry as she loses those closest to her - and there's no final apology from the author. This is what happened back then, this is how criminals were treated, and she isn't going to sugar-coat it for modern readers. There's a happy ending of sorts, but not for everyone and there's no promise that what Mary went through made anything better for future transportees. Of course, we know that eventually it did and a long time has passed, but it still makes uncomfortable reading in places.<br /><br />Fab read - can't wait to read more.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2770791511075059733" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

It was an eye-opener to read how hard their experience was, especially if you were a women as they were greatly outnumbered by the men and didn't have the same opportunities.<br/>Mary was a great character and I got caught up in her story and her resilience to survive.</span>

  <span id="freeText7476404921876711557" style="display:none">A decent book, very hard to rate. I liked it, to a certain degree, but there was always something that kept me at arm's length. I can't describe exactly what my issue was, other than it felt like I was reading a book written by a teenager. I liked the book enough to want to read others by this author, but this short book still took me several long days to trudge though. It just didn't click for me.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer1958492699132235515">Yes. My last read of Jan.2017 is successfully finished at the last minute. <br/><br/>•	18th Century Victorian Crime &Punishment in England.<br/><br/>•	This is the middle of 18th Century &London is the jail capital of Europe. The jails stink, but not as much as the English justice system. It is unpredictable, disorganized &the toughest it has ever been.   <span id="freeText1958492699132235515" style="display:none">Yes. My last read of Jan.2017 is successfully finished at the last minute. <br /><br />•	18th Century Victorian Crime &amp;Punishment in England.<br /><br />•	This is the middle of 18th Century &amp;London is the jail capital of Europe. The jails stink, but not as much as the English justice system. It is unpredictable, disorganized &amp;the toughest it has ever been. There is not really a police force, levels of crime are high &amp;there is a need for low cost penalties. Punishments range from standing in the pillory, to branding, whipping &amp;burning. Death is the penalty for over 200 offences. Even children are being hanged. This is not a good time to be on trial. Some, such as treason or murder, were serious crimes, but others were what we would call minor offences. For example, the death sentence could be passed for picking pockets or stealing food. These were the kinds of crime likely to be committed by people in most need, at a time when many families lived in poverty. Towards the end of 1700's, the number of people hanged for petty crimes was causing public unrest. <br /><br />•	Historical novel.<br />•	Detailed True story of Mary Bryant.<br />•	Mary Broad-Bryant was born in a fishing family &amp;to earn more she left home to seek work in different part of England. She became involved in minor robberies.. She, along with her other friends were caught &amp;sentenced to hang. She was transported to Australia &amp;delivered a baby girl whom she called her Charlotte; name of the ship. Soon after she got married with William Bryant who was also on that ship; a convicted smuggler! &amp;had a son together; Emanuel. They try to escape… going through defeats &amp;obstacles, great challenges (physically &amp;emotionally), she manages to keep their survival instinct alive all the way her journey. She was a fighter.<br /><br />•	A basket of thanks to the skilled author: #Lesley_Pearse who amused us with this great true story.<br />•	&amp;a world of gratitude to the beautiful girl who I never met her in real but she has lightened my world of knowledge &amp;who her birthday is in the present day: wishing you beautiful years ahead full of health, love, wisdom &amp;patience.<br /><br /><br />•	By reading “Remember Me” I remember you @nadirasworld (Nadira Sultana) . I thank you for gifting such a precious book &amp;giving me a chance for reading one of your top ten rated favorite books.</span>

<div id="review_715354353" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/715354353" />
    <a title="Veronikah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5470694-veronikah"><img alt="Veronikah" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1498472323p2/5470694.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/715354353?book_show_action=true">Sep 09, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Veronikah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Veronikah" href="/user/show/5470694-veronikah">Veronikah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9789892303178" href="/book/show/6298008-nunca-me-esque-as">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5470694-veronikah?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5470694-veronikah?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer715354353" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2982451181444167576">2.5 Stars<br/><br/>Remember Me is an interesting book. It's worth the read. Don't think it's bad just because of the 2 stars over there. The thing is, I had a like/hate relationship with this book. There were moments when I just wanted to close it and never read again. But I wanted to see how it ended, I wanted to see if Mary had that deserved ending, and so I continued.<br/><br/>This book tells the story of Mary Bryant, one of the first escapees of the Australian penal colonies. Mary existed, the main characters t</span>
  <span id="freeText2982451181444167576" style="display:none">2.5 Stars<br /><br />Remember Me is an interesting book. It's worth the read. Don't think it's bad just because of the 2 stars over there. The thing is, I had a like/hate relationship with this book. There were moments when I just wanted to close it and never read again. But I wanted to see how it ended, I wanted to see if Mary had that deserved ending, and so I continued.<br /><br />This book tells the story of Mary Bryant, one of the first escapees of the Australian penal colonies. Mary existed, the main characters that surround her also existed and the horrors she went through as well. It follows her life from the moment she was caught because of highway robbery (or something like that), through her times at the prison-ships, through her voyage to the faraway Australia, through her life at the colony, through her escape and being caught until the moment she disappeared from any records (<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ because after she was granted her pardon and returned to Cornwall nothing else is know of her <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>).<br /><br />To be honest, this isn't a book anyone can read. The things she went through are horrible and frightening. Thankfully Pearse's writing can get the message and the picture through without needing extra details. With just the right words Pearse made sure the reader knew how things happened, whether they were bad or good.<br />It's a book that can make you feel thankful you live in the 21st century, where even in most prisons there is some humanity (sure, some criminals deserve nothing else but to suffer like those prisoners from Mary's time, but not all of them).<br /><br />I won't be reading this book again though. One time experience was enough. Some books just aren't meant to be read more than once, and Remember Me is one of those.<br /><br />But still, if you're interested in knowing a bit more on how prisons worked in the 18th century and how the first colonies in Australia worked, this book teaches you a lot.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2982451181444167576" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Thangia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25387489-thangia"><img alt="Thangia" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer758953660" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16059936074128906027">Despite this book being incredibly sad, I loved reading it. The plot was very good (even though its based on a true story) and I love how Lesley Pearse gave depth to all the characters and how well she described the prisons and Australia so well, to the point I almost felt I was there with Mary experiencing everything with her (I know that sounds incredibly cliche but its true). Its one of those books that are quite emotionally draining so I don't think I could bring myself to read it again. I h</span>
  <span id="freeText16059936074128906027" style="display:none">Despite this book being incredibly sad, I loved reading it. The plot was very good (even though its based on a true story) and I love how Lesley Pearse gave depth to all the characters and how well she described the prisons and Australia so well, to the point I almost felt I was there with Mary experiencing everything with her (I know that sounds incredibly cliche but its true). Its one of those books that are quite emotionally draining so I don't think I could bring myself to read it again. I have to admit though, that the ending was a bit rubbish. I know Lesley Pearse was following true accounts but I wish she sort of made up an ending to please her readers. I do think she writes in the end that she wanted to make up the ending but felt like she shouldn't (if my memory serves well) so I can forgive her for this. Still a brilliant book, it gives an amazing insight of how really hard prison life was back then and I would definitely recommend it. </span>

It was also immensely interesting to learn about Australia's convict beginnings. <br /><br />It also makes you realise how lucky we are to live in civilised societies. I would just love to know how Mary's story really ended up, I hope for one that she had more children and got to enjoy the family life she so dearly wanted. <br /><br /><br /><br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer16990073676205000443">I've only read one other book by Lesley Pearse. It was a book, in Swedish, that I found in a flea market and bought because it sounded interesting. I've read it at least three times, despite its' size, and I love it equally every time. I wish to reread it all the time, and I feel like it's time for that soon.<br/><br/>So, what about this one. I found it in my audio book app and thought it sounded intriguing, so despite the length of it I decided to download and listen to it. And that's not a decision I've</span>
  <span id="freeText16990073676205000443" style="display:none">I've only read one other book by Lesley Pearse. It was a book, in Swedish, that I found in a flea market and bought because it sounded interesting. I've read it at least three times, despite its' size, and I love it equally every time. I wish to reread it all the time, and I feel like it's time for that soon.<br /><br />So, what about this one. I found it in my audio book app and thought it sounded intriguing, so despite the length of it I decided to download and listen to it. And that's not a decision I've regretted even once (except for maybe that time I had to look myself in the bathroom cause I was crying too much).<br /><br />I loved this. It might be considered a slow read. But when you have 8 hours at work each day, a good book helps a lot. As I said, I cried a lot towards the end. Even though I'm used to having tears in my eyes at work (because of the books I listen to), I'm not used to being blinded by the tears. So that's that. I loved the book, I want someone I know to read it so that we can discuss it.</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8625473-laureen?shelf=historical">historical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8625473-laureen?shelf=australian">australian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8625473-laureen?shelf=library-mp3-audio">library-mp3-audio</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8625473-laureen?shelf=convicts">convicts</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2271993561" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1533643920215506387">Rounded down to 3.5. Great story of survival. I must say I was surprised by how much of this story was true. However I think Mary's chatacter was just a little far fetched. There was a bit too much modern day feminism depicted which I thought was a stretch. Most women of the era did have to be very resourceful but men would have had to be just as resourceful because manly pride was a big deal. However, so was bigotry. If Mary did, in fact, overcome the general traditions of the time, then, yes, </span>
  <span id="freeText1533643920215506387" style="display:none">Rounded down to 3.5. Great story of survival. I must say I was surprised by how much of this story was true. However I think Mary's chatacter was just a little far fetched. There was a bit too much modern day feminism depicted which I thought was a stretch. Most women of the era did have to be very resourceful but men would have had to be just as resourceful because manly pride was a big deal. However, so was bigotry. If Mary did, in fact, overcome the general traditions of the time, then, yes, indeed, she was a remarkable woman. I just think men of that time would have most likely resented her deeply. I have to recommend this novel because there is important history here to be discovered and the author did well to put this story together with much research. <br /><br />It is a story that makes one really recognize that Australia's settlement came with much suffering, deprivation and death. </span>
  <a data-text-id="1533643920215506387" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('gs8J8KsVr2EBq6i9S90rz8xap4r2Y4TkftHNwm6mhOPg8ctMKgs6qUC8FduFbp48KdNnfZ9O2TjDknB2v/zVwA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('yDix1B+8bsJXeX8clpBrAkHC4Pd84l/+bStwCd415weqBnNonqL7ChZuwnpYI97xpEsgABXPAiLQaM29D2+2JA==')})
  }

From the moment they met in college, best friends Adele Brannon and Kamryn Matika thought nothing could come between them—until Adele did the unthinkable and slept with Kamryn’s fiancé, Nate. Now, after years of silence, the two women are reuniting, and Adele has a stunning request for her old friend: she wants Kamryn to adopt her five-year-old daughter, Tegan.Besides the difference in skin color—many will assume that headstrong, impulsive Kamryn is Tegan’s nanny—there’s the inconvenient truth that Kamryn is wholly unprepared to take care of anyone, especially someone who reminds her so much of Nate. With crises brewing at work and her love life in shambles, can Kamryn somehow become the mother a little girl needs her to be? In My Best Friend’s Girl, Dorothy Koomson takes us on a warm and wondrous journey through laughter and tears, forgiveness and hope—and the enduring love forged by the unlikeliest of       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/458937.Lesley_Pearse">About Lesley Pearse</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/458937.Lesley_Pearse"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1261863858p3/458937.jpg);'></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer12472696362112765358">Lesley Pearse is one of the UK's best-loved novelists with fans across the globe and sales of over 2 million copies of her books to date. A true storyteller and a master of gripping storylines that keep the reader hooked from beginning to end, Pearse introduces you to characters that it is impossible not to care about or forget. There is no formula to her books or easily defined genre. Whether cri</span>
  <span id="freeText12472696362112765358" style="display:none">Lesley Pearse is one of the UK's best-loved novelists with fans across the globe and sales of over 2 million copies of her books to date. A true storyteller and a master of gripping storylines that keep the reader hooked from beginning to end, Pearse introduces you to characters that it is impossible not to care about or forget. There is no formula to her books or easily defined genre. Whether crime as in 'Till We Meet Again', historical adventure like 'Never Look Back', or the passionately emotive 'Trust Me', based on the true-life scandal of British child migrants sent to Australia in the post war period, she engages the reader completely.<br />Truth is often stranger than fiction and Lesley's life has been as packed with drama as her books. She was three when her mother died under tragic circumstances. Her father was away at sea and it was only when a neighbour saw Lesley and her brother playing outside without coats on that suspicion was aroused - their mother had been dead for some time. With her father in the Royal Marines, Lesley and her older brother spent three years in grim orphanages before her father remarried - a veritable dragon of an ex army nurse - and Lesley and her older brother were brought home again, to be joined by two other children who were later adopted by her father and stepmother, and a continuing stream of foster children. The impact of constant change and uncertainty in Lesley's early years is reflected in one of the recurring themes in her books: what happens to those who are emotionally damaged as children. It was an extraordinary childhood and in all her books, Lesley has skilfully married the pain and unhappiness of her early experiences with a unique gift for storytelling.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12472696362112765358" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>
